## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population P and time t, which is the core problem in population ecology. The relationship typically involves density-dependent feedback mechanisms where growth rate depends on current population size.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth, common in tumor/population modeling)
- Theta-logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (1 + c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 + P) * (c2 + P) (cubic dependence capturing extinction threshold and carrying capacity)
- Von Bertalanffy-type rate: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 + c2 * P (differential growth-loss scaling)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized growth with flexible inflection point)
- Time-varying exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate changing with time)
- Harvesting/immigration model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) + c2 (logistic with constant immigration/harvesting)
- Power-law growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Oscillatory growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal/periodic environmental forcing)
- Delayed density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence on P (dP_dt ∝ P) → density-independent exponential growth phase
- Quadratic term P² with opposite sign to linear P term → density-dependent logistic-type regulation with carrying capacity
- Cubic polynomial in P → Allee effect or bistability with multiple equilibria (extinction and carrying capacity)
- P * log(P) structure → Gompertz-type growth with asymmetric approach to carrying capacity
- Fractional power P**c with 0<c<1 → surface-area-limited or diffusion-limited growth processes
- Multiplicative time-dependent modulation (e.g., sin(c*t)) → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on growth
- Constant additive term independent of P → immigration, stocking, or constant harvesting effects
- Product of multiple linear factors in P → multiple critical population thresholds (Allee threshold, carrying capacity)
- Ratio of polynomials in P (e.g., P²/(P²+c)) → cooperative or inhibitory density-dependent effects with saturation
